### Post by fedex1993 on 2008-01-31
Jfebruary 2008 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

*To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.
__________________

---

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-01-31
> **~LoKe said:**
> Can I get your irssi config?

Here it is:

```
servers = (
  {
  }
);

chatnets = {
  {
  };
};

channels = (
  {
  }
);

aliases = {
  J = "join";
  DATE = "time";
  HOST = "userhost";
  W = "whois $0 $0";
  N = "names";
  T = "topic";
  C = "scrollback clear";
  K = "kick";
  KB = "kickban";
  KN = "knockout";
  B = "ban";
  UB = "unban";
  IG = "ignore";
  UNIG = "unignore";
  WC = "window close";
  ID = "quote nickserv identify";
  RUN = "SCRIPT LOAD";
  UPTIME = "eval exec - expr `date +%s` - \\$F | awk '{print \"Irssi uptime: \"int(\\\\\\$1/3600/24)\"d \"int(\\\\\\$1/3600%24)\"h \"int(\\\\\\$1/60%60)\"m \"int(\\\\\\$1%60)\"s\" }'";
  CALC = "exec - if which bc &>/dev/null\\; then echo '$*' | bc | awk '{print \"$*=\"$$1}'\\; else echo bc was not found\\; fi";
  Q = "QUERY";
};

statusbar = {

  items = {
    prompt = "{prompt $[.15]itemname}";
    prompt_empty = "{prompt $winname}";

    separator = "%G--------------------------------------------------------------------------------";
    separator2 = "%G--------------------------------------------------------------------------------%N";
  };

  default = {
    topic = { disabled = "yes"; };
    window = { disabled = "yes"; };
    window_inact = { disabled = "yes"; };

    separator = {
      type = "root";
      placement = "bottom";
      position = "0";
      visible = "always";
      items = { separator = { }; separator2 = { }; };
    };

    prompt = {
      type = "root";
      placement = "bottom";
      position = "100";
      visible = "always";
      items = {
        prompt = { priority = "-1"; };
        prompt_empty = { priority = "-1"; };
        input = { priority = "10"; };
      };
    };

    awl_0 = {
      items = {
        barstart = { priority = "100"; };
        awl_0 = { };
        barend = { priority = "100"; alignment = "right"; };
      };
    };
  };
};

settings = {
  core = {
    real_name = "";
    user_name = "";
    nick = "";
    quit_message = "";
  };
  "perl/core/scripts" = {
    awl_display_key = "$H$N:$C$S ";
    awl_automode = "sbar";
  };
  "fe-common/core" = {
    timestamps = "yes";
    show_nickmode = "yes";
    theme = "minimalist";
  };
  "irc/core" = { skip_motd = "yes"; };
  "fe-text" = { actlist_sort = "refnum"; };
};
logs = { };
```

There is also a minimal.theme file and scripts involved in this though, I got them from phraok. Just let me know if you need those as well.

---

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-01-31
> **~LoKe said:**
> Thanks!  I don't think I need a theme, I just didn't have a channel list at the bottom of irssi, nor did I have the userlist on the side.

You need the scripts for that. Make a "scripts" folder inside your .irssi folder, and an "autorun" folder inside that scripts folder. Then download these into the autorun folder: [http://phraok.free.fr/config/irssi/scripts/autorun/](http://phraok.free.fr/config/irssi/scripts/autorun/)

The channel list should then be working; to get the userlist on the side you have to type "/NICKLIST SCREEN" in irssi. (This will only work with the scripts)

---

### Post by el mariachi on 2008-01-31
showing the feel of my desktop this month.
I haven't changed the themes (yet)
btw: does anyone know if: first- is it possible to use an image for the menubar (file, edit,...) with the Aurora engine
and second: if it is, how do i do it?

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-01-31
> **el mariachi said:**
> showing the feel of my desktop this month.
I haven't changed the themes (yet)
btw: does anyone know if: first- is it possible to use an image for the menubar (file, edit,...) with the Aurora engine
and second: if it is, how do i do it?

Oh, people always kill me when they show something red...

I believe the Pixmap engine is the only one able to allow images by default. BUT you can try your luck with the .gtkrc-2.0 file on your home folder, or create a menubar.rc and include it at the gtkrc file of the Aurora theme you're using...

When I felt I needed a pixmap under my Xfce-panel, for instance, I put this in my .gtkrc-2.0 file:

```
style "panel"
{
bg[NORMAL] = "#000000"
#bg_pixmap[NORMAL] = "background.png"
fg[NORMAL] = "#FFFFFF"
}

widget_class "*Panel*" style "panel"
widget "*Panel*" style "panel"
class "*Panel*" style "panel"
```


How about trying to change those classes to those related to menubars?

---

### Post by sunexplodes on 2008-01-31

### Post by rainwalker on 2008-02-01
Hey how do you post an image as a small thumbnail, but have it link to a larger one?

---

### Post by ayoli on 2008-02-01
> **rainwalker said:**
> Hey how do you post an image as a small thumbnail, but have it link to a larger one?
Insert an image (the thumbnail) with the image button, then select the whole line (the image url + the IMG tags and us the button "insert link" to give a link to the larger image.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-02-01
> **rainwalker said:**
> Hey how do you post an image as a small thumbnail, but have it link to a larger one?

Upload it to ImageShack, Picoodle, All You Can Upload, etc. They will give you several pieces of code to post here. The most indicated will probably say "for Forums (primary)" or something. You copy and paste it here.

---

### Post by Nythain on 2008-02-01
> **rainwalker said:**
> Hey how do you post an image as a small thumbnail, but have it link to a larger one?
or you could just you know, click on "Manage Attatchments" in the "Addidtional Options" and upload the pic as a post attatchment... it will show the thumbnail in the post, then just show the big when you click on it, without the hassle of being directed to another site, and waiting for all thier adds and popups to finish before finally slowly loading the large image :P

### Post by ayoli on 2008-02-01
> **el mariachi said:**
> showing the feel of my desktop this month.
I haven't changed the themes (yet)
btw: does anyone know if: first- is it possible to use an image for the menubar (file, edit,...) with the Aurora engine
and second: if it is, how do i do it?
I don't think that the aurora engine itself uses images.
There is the bg_pixmap[NORMAL]=/path/to/png way.
Or use the pixmap engine only for the menu and aurora egine for the rest.
Theme like elegant one use pixmap for the menu you can use it as a base.

### Post by el mariachi on 2008-02-02
```
VERSION = 2.4

BG_COLOR    = "0x000000"
TASK_COLOR      = "0xffffff"
FOCUSED_COLOR   = "0x49ccdf"
SHADED_COLOR    = "0x808080"
MINIMIZED_COLOR = "0x808080"
DESKTOP_COLOR   = "0xffffff"
CLOCK_COLOR    = "0xFFFFFF"
LINE_COLOR    = "0x000000"

TASK_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xFFFFFF"
FOCUSED_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xFFFFFF"
SHADED_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xFFFFFF"
MINIMIZED_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xFFFFFF" 
DESKTOP_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xFFFFFF"
CLOCK_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xffffff"

P_LOCATION    = 1        # panel placement: 0 = top, 1 = bottom
P_WIDTH        = 1016        # panel width: 0 = full screen width
P_START        = 4        # starting X coordinate of the panel
P_SPACER    = 7        # spacing between panel objects
P_HEIGHT    = 20
P_L_BUFF        = 0
P_R_BUFF        = 0
P_T_BUFF        = 5
P_B_BUFF        = 5

I_HEIGHT    = 16        # application icon height
I_WIDTH        = 16        # application icon Width 
APPL_I_HEIGHT    = 16        # application launcher icon height
APPL_I_WIDTH    = 16        # application launcher icon width
TRAY_I_HEIGHT    = 16        # system tray icon height
TRAY_I_WIDTH    = 16        # system tray icon width

CLOCK_FORMAT    = "%H:%M"
CLOCK_DELAY    = 20

HIDE_LIST    = ["netwmpager"]
HIDDEN_SIZE     = 2

FONT        = "DejaVu Sans-Book:size=8"

SHOWALL        = 0        # show windows from all desktops
SHOWMINIMIZED    = 0        # only show minimized windows
SHADE        = 200

ABOVE        = 1        # panel is always above other apps
APPICONS    = 0        # show application icons
AUTOHIDE    = 0        # autohide uses the CLOCK_DELAY timer above
SHADOWS        = 0        # show text shadows
SHOWLINES    = 0        # show object seperation lines
SHOWBORDER    = 1        # show a border around the panel

DESKTOP_NAMES    = ["main", "www", "media", "misc", "term"]

# Order

DESKTOP        = 1
TASKS        = 2
CLOCK        = 4
TRAY        = 3
LAUNCHER    = 0

def desktopButtonEvent(pp, button):
    pass

def taskButtonEvent(pp, button, task):
    if button == 1:
        pp.taskFocus(task)
    elif button == 2:
        task.obj.destroy()
    elif button == 3:
        pp.toggleShade(task)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.taskRaise(task, focus=1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.taskLower(task, focus=0)

def clockButtonEvent(pp, button):
    pp.showDesktop()

def panelButtonEvent(pp, button):
    pass
```
here you go :D

### Post by NoWhereMan on 2008-02-02
The first screen is to show you my awesome wallpaper :D, which is a Turner's work of art which should be entitled "Rain, Steam and Speed" or "The Great Western Railway"; I've customized the default ubuntu gdm theme to use this wallpaper too, instead of the usual brownish background

The second is a completely custom version of *MurrinaSunshine* (kudos to the orginal author, you can find the original theme on gnome-look), which I couldn't make still look as I wanted (the checkboxes in update-manager and in menus are too dark)...

btw, I'll attach here if you want to try (and maybe fix it :D)

The third shows off the gtk theme I'm currently using which is **Murrina-TangoGrey** (you can find it on gnome-look)

The window border (metacity) comes bundled with Murrina-TangoGrey; xcompmgr as composite manager

Suggestions welcomed :)

gtkrc follows

```
#########################################################################
# Murrina STILLNONAME :D by NoWhereMan | www.nowhereland.it
# based on:
# Murrina Sunshine by Pakos - admin@allucinator.pl | http://allucinator.pl #
#########################################################################

gtk-button-images = 0 
gtk-icon-sizes = "panel-menu=16,16:panel=16,16:gtk-button=16,16:gtk-large-toolbar=16,16"
gtk-menu-images = 0
style "theme-default"
{
  GtkButton      ::default_border    = { 0, 0, 0, 0 }
  GtkRange       ::trough_border     = 0
  GtkPaned       ::handle_size       = 6
  GtkRange       ::slider_width      = 14
  GtkRange       ::stepper_size      = 14

  GtkScrollbar   ::min_slider_length = 30
  GtkCheckButton ::indicator_size    = 10
  GtkRadioButton ::indicator_size    = 10
  GtkMenuBar     ::internal-padding  = 0
  GtkTreeView    ::expander_size     = 14
  GtkExpander    ::expander_size     = 16
  GtkScale       ::slider-length     = 16

  
  
  xthickness = 1
  ythickness = 1

  fg[NORMAL]        = "#222222" 
  fg[PRELIGHT]      = "#E2CE94"
  fg[SELECTED]      = "#E2CE94"
  fg[ACTIVE]        = "#222222" 
  fg[INSENSITIVE]   = "#eeeeee" #? 

  bg[NORMAL]        = "#fffefc" 
  bg[PRELIGHT]      = "#222222" #"#fffefc"
  bg[SELECTED]	    = "#fffefc" 
  bg[INSENSITIVE]   = "#fffefc" 
  bg[ACTIVE]        = "#fffefc" 

  base[NORMAL]      = "#fffefc" 
  base[PRELIGHT]    = "#fffefc" #?
  base[ACTIVE]      = "#f6efe0" 
  base[SELECTED]    = "#222222" 
  base[INSENSITIVE] = "#fffefc"

  text[NORMAL]      = "#555555" 
  text[PRELIGHT]    = "#E2CE94" 
  text[ACTIVE]      = "#E2CE94" 
  text[SELECTED]    = "#555555"
  text[INSENSITIVE] = "#eeeeee"

  engine "murrine" 
  {
menuitemstyle = 0 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy, 2 = striped
	 scrollbar_color     = "#f6efe0"
	 scrollbarstyle		= 0 
	 contrast 			   = 1.0
	 menustyle = 0
glazestyle = 0 # 0 = flat hilight, 1 = curved hilight, 2 = concave style
	 menubarstyle = 0 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy, 2 = gradient, 3 = striped
	 menubaritemstyle = 0 # 0 = menuitem look, 1 = button look
menuitemstyle = 0 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy, 2 = striped
	 listviewheaderstyle = 0 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy
	 listviewstyle = 1
	 gradients				= FALSE
roundness = 0
    animation = TRUE # FALSE = disabled, TRUE = enabled
    hilight_ratio = 0.909090
  }
}


style "theme-wide" = "theme-default"
{
  xthickness = 2
  ythickness = 2
}

style "theme-wider" = "theme-default"
{
  xthickness = 2
  ythickness = 2
}

style "theme-entry" = "theme-wider"
{
  bg[SELECTED]	    = "#222222"
}

style "theme-button" = "theme-wider"
{
  xthickness = 2
  ythickness = 0
  bg[NORMAL]        = "#fffefc" 
  bg[INSENSITIVE]   = "#fffefc"
  # bg[PRELIGHT]      = "#E2CE94" 
  bg[ACTIVE]	     = "#E2CE94"
  #text[PRELIGHT]    = "#222222" 
 
}


style "theme-notebook" = "theme-wide"
{
  bg[NORMAL]      = "#fffefc" 
  bg[INSENSITIVE] = "#ffffff"
  bg[SELECTED]    = "#E2CE94" 
}

style "theme-tasklist" = "theme-default"
{
  xthickness = 4
  ythickness = 2
}

style "theme-menu" = "theme-default"
{
  xthickness = 2
  ythickness = 2
  #bg[NORMAL] = "#000000"
  
  
}

style "theme-menu-item" = "theme-default"
{
  ythickness = 3
  #fg[NORMAL] = "#696866" 
  fg[PRELIGHT] = "#E2CE94" 
  fg[SELECTED] = "#E2CE94" 
  #fg[INSENSITIVE]      = "#333333"
  bg[SELECTED]	    = "#222222"
  #text[NORMAL]      = "#d0d0d0" 
  text[PRELIGHT]    = "#E2CE94" 

}
  

style "theme-menubar" = "theme-default"
{
  bg[NORMAL] = "#000000"
  text[NORMAL] = "#E2CE94" 
}

style "theme-menubar-item"
{
  ythickness = 2
  fg[NORMAL] = "#E2CE94" 
  bg[PRELIGHT] = "#222222" 
  bg[SELECTED] = "#222222" 
}

style "theme-tree" = "theme-default"
{
  xthickness = 2
  ythickness = 2
  text[SELECTED]    = "#000000"
}

style "theme-frame-title" = "theme-default"
{

  fg[NORMAL] = "#222222"
}

style "theme-tooltips" = "theme-default"
{
  xthickness = 2
  ythickness = 2
  bg[NORMAL] = "#fffefc"
}

style "theme-progressbar" = "theme-wide"
{
  xthickness = 2
  ythickness = 2
  fg[PRELIGHT]  = "#222222"
  bg[NORMAL]        = "#fffefc"
  bg[SELECTED]	    = "#E2CE94"
}

style "theme-combo" = "theme-button"
{

}

style "metacity-frame"
{
  # Normal base color
  #bg[NORMAL]  = "#bbbbbb"

  # Unfocused title background color
  #bg[INSENSITIVE]  = { 0.8, 0.8, 0.8 }

  # Unfocused title text color
  #fg[INSENSITIVE]  = { 1.55, 1.55, 1.55 }

  # Focused icon color
  #fg[NORMAL]  = { 0.2, 0.2, 0.2 }

  # Focused title background color
  bg[SELECTED]  = "#000000"
  #base[ACTIVE]  = "#f2f2f2"

  # Focused title text color
  fg[SELECTED]  = "#ffffff"
}
class "MetaFrames" 	  style "metacity-frame"
class "GtkWindow"      style "metacity-frame"


style "inactivetext2"
{


  #fg[PRELIGHT] 		= "#c13bb0"
  #fg[NORMAL]    ="#c13bb0"
  
}

widget_class "*.<GtkMenuItem>.*" style "inactivetext2"

# PANEL
style "panel"{
  xthickness            			= 2
  ythickness            			= 2
	bg[NORMAL]   = "#222222"
	fg[NORMAL]   = "#222222" 
	text[NORMAL] = "#d0d0d0" 
}

style "panelbuttons"{
  xthickness            			= 0
  ythickness            			= 0
    bg[NORMAL] 		= "#222222"
    bg[ACTIVE]		= "#222222" 
    bg[SELECTED]	= "#d0d0d0" 
    bg[PRELIGHT]	= "#222222"
    
    fg[NORMAL]		= "#d0d0d0"
    fg[ACTIVE]		= "#E2CE94" 
    fg[PRELIGHT]	= "#E2CE94"
}
class "*Panel*" style "panel"
widget_class "*Panel*GtkToggleButton" style "panelbuttons"
widget_class "*Panel*Button" style "panelbuttons"
widget_class "*Panel*b*" style "panelbuttons"


# widget styles
class "GtkWidget"      style "theme-default"
class "GtkButton"      style "theme-button" #button
class "GtkScale"       style "theme-button"
class "GtkCombo"       style "theme-button"
class "GtkRange"       style "theme-wide"
class "GtkFrame"       style "theme-wide"
class "GtkMenu"        style "theme-menu"
class "GtkEntry"       style "theme-entry"
class "GtkMenuItem"    style "theme-menu-item"
class "GtkNotebook"    style "theme-notebook"
class "GtkProgressBar" style "theme-progressbar"
class "*MenuBar*"      style "theme-menubar"

widget_class "*MenuItem.*" style "theme-menu-item"
widget_class "*MenuBar.*"  style "theme-menubar-item"

# combobox stuff
widget_class "*.GtkComboBox.GtkButton" style "theme-combo"
widget_class "*.GtkCombo.GtkButton"    style "theme-combo"
# tooltips stuff
widget_class "*.tooltips.*.GtkToggleButton" style "theme-tasklist"
widget "gtk-tooltips" style "theme-tooltips"

# treeview stuff
widget_class "*.GtkTreeView.GtkButton" style "theme-tree"
widget_class "*.GtkTreeView.GtkToggleButton" style "theme-tree"
widget_class "*.GtkCTree.GtkButton" style "theme-tree"
widget_class "*.GtkCTree.GtkToggleButton" style "theme-tree"
widget_class "*.GtkList.GtkButton" style "theme-tree"
widget_class "*.GtkList.GtkButton" style "theme-tree"
widget_class "*.GtkCList.GtkButton" style "theme-tree"
widget_class "*.GtkCList.GtkToggleButton" style "theme-tree"
widget_class "*.GtkFrame.GtkLabel" style "theme-frame-title"

# notebook stuff
widget_class "*.GtkNotebook.*.GtkEventBox" style "theme-notebook"
widget_class "*.GtkNotebook.*.GtkViewport" style "theme-notebook"

```

### Post by NoWhereMan on 2008-02-03
> **shearn89 said:**
> How did you get the pattern in the background of your file manager? Is that nautilus?

yep, nautilus in spatial mode, the background came from MurrinaNatural, but I'm attaching it at your convenience :)

You can set it to all the nautilus windows by editing the gconf key at /app/nautilus/preferences/background_filename and setting it to the file path of this background file :)

bye

### Post by semperfiguy on 2008-02-03
Here is my .xdefaults file
```
urxvt*geometry:  85x22
urxvt*fading:    15
urxvt*tintColor: #000000
urxvt*shading:   20
urxvt*inheritPixmap: True
urxvt*scrollBar: False
urxvt*urlLauncher:      firefox

urxvt*font: xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=11:antialias=true:hinting=true
urxvt*boldFont: xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=11:antialias=true:bold:hinting=true
urxvt*italicFont: xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=11:antialias=true:italic:autohint=true:hinting=true
urxvt*bolditalicFont: xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=11:antialias=true:bold:italic:autohint=true:hinting=true

urxvt*background:  #000000
urxvt*foreground:  #ffffff
! Black + DarkGrey
urxvt*color0:       #000000
urxvt*color8:       #666666
! DarkRed + Red
urxvt*color1:       #b45151
urxvt*color9:       #fe8686
! DarkGreen + Green
urxvt*color2:       #65d827
urxvt*color10:      #a2ea86
! DarkYellow + Yellow
urxvt*color3:       Khaki3
urxvt*color11:      #efe58b
! DarkBlue + Blue
urxvt*color4:       #2797d8
urxvt*color12:      #86cdea
! DarkMangenta + Mangenta
urxvt*color5:       #aa6eaf
urxvt*color13:      #cb96ce
!DarkCyan + Cyan
urxvt*color6:       #418179
urxvt*color14:      #71bebe
! LightGrey + White
urxvt*color7:       #bebebe
urxvt*color15:      #ffffff

```

My music player is Sonata.  It's a mpd client.

### Post by El_Belgicano on 2008-02-03
@Ayoli: How did you make your console look like that?

---

### Post by ayoli on 2008-02-03
> **El_Belgicano said:**
> @Ayoli: How did you make your console look like that?

Here's my .bashrc, but actually it's a bit tricky and do not work prpoerly when using history (with arrows up and down) :
```
#!/bin/bash

#   termwide prompt
#      by Giles - created 2 November 98
#	   last tweaked by ayoli - 17 oct 2007
#
#   The idea here is to have the upper line of this two line prompt 
#   always be the width of your term.  Do this by calculating the
#   width of the text elements, and putting in fill as appropriate
#   or left-truncating $PWD.
#

function prompt_command {

TERMWIDTH=${COLUMNS}

#   Calculate the width of the prompt:

hostnam=$(echo -n $HOSTNAME | sed -e "s/[\.].*//")
#   "whoami" and "pwd" include a trailing newline
usernam=$(whoami)
let usersize=$(echo -n $usernam | wc -c | tr -d " ")
newPWD="${PWD}"
let pwdsize=$(echo -n ${newPWD} | wc -c | tr -d " ")
#   Add all the accessories below ...
let promptsize=$(echo -n "--(0000:day,00 mon YY.${usernam}@${hostnam})---(${PWD})--" \
                 | wc -c | tr -d " ")
let fillsize=${TERMWIDTH}-${promptsize}
fill=""
B="\033(0q\033(B"
while [ "$fillsize" -gt "0" ] 
do 
   fill="${fill}$(echo -e $B)"
   let fillsize=${fillsize}-1
done

if [ "$fillsize" -lt "0" ]
then
   let cut=3-${fillsize}
   newPWD="...$(echo -n $PWD | sed -e "s/\(^.\{$cut\}\)\(.*\)/\2/")"
fi
}

PROMPT_COMMAND=prompt_command

function termwide {

local GRAY="\[\033[1;30m\]"
local LIGHT_GRAY="\[\033[0;37m\]"
local WHITE="\[\033[1;37m\]"
local NO_COLOUR="\[\033[0m\]"
local RED="\[\033[1;31m\]"
local GREEN="\[\033[1;32m\]"

local CYAN="\[\033[1;36m\]"
local BLUE="\[\033[1;34m\]"
local YELLOW="\[\033[1;33m\]"

case $TERM in
    xterm*)
        TITLEBAR='\[\033]0;\u@\h:\w\007\]'
        ;;
    *)
        TITLEBAR=""
        ;;
esac

PS1="$TITLEBAR\
$GREEN\[\033(0l\033(B\]-(\
$BLUE\$(date +%H%M)$GREEN:$BLUE\$(date \"+%a,%d %b %y\")\
$BLUE.\${usernam}$GREEN@$BLUE\${hostnam}\
${GREEN})\[\033(0q\033(B\]\[\033(0q\033(B\]\${fill}${GREEN}\[\033(0q\033(B\](\
$BLUE\${newPWD}\
$GREEN)\[\033(0q\033(B\]\[\033(0q\033(B\]\
\n\
$GREEN\[\033(0m\033(B\]\[\033(0q\033(B\](\
$BLUE\$$GREEN)\[\033(0q\033(B\]\
$GREEN>\
$CYAN " 

PS2="$BLUE-$YELLOW-$YELLOW-$NO_COLOUR "

}

# load prompt
termwide
```

### Post by fwojciec on 2008-02-05
Why does everybody want to get rid of conky so badly?  If you can make it work conky is a much more efficient solution than bash scripts -- it's written in C so it's going to be much faster and lighter than multiple bash scripts that are re-run every couple of seconds.

---

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-05
> **fwojciec said:**
> Why does everybody needs to get rid of conky so badly?  If you can make it work conky is a much more efficient solution than bash scripts -- it's written in C so it's going to be much faster and lighter than multiple bash scripts that are re-run every couple of seconds.

The problem is that ubuntu doesn't have a conky-cli package (well, nothing besides Arch has as far as I know), which is why I think conky isn't updating when put into the statusbar.

---

### Post by fwojciec on 2008-02-05
> **Gigamo said:**
> The problem is that ubuntu doesn't have a conky-cli package (well, nothing besides Arch has as far as I know), which is why I think conky isn't updating when put into the statusbar.

EDIT: Nevermind - I just tried conky with awesome and for some reason it doesn't work properly.  It's strange though -- the exact same command works perfectly fine in openbox.  Must be something weird with awesome.

### Post by hellion0 on 2008-02-05
This month, we have a desktop from altaria, my testing laptop, running Xubuntu 7.10.

[[IMG]http://img267.imageshack.us/img267/5751/200802051504181024x768ssy4.th.png[/IMG]](http://img267.imageshack.us/my.php?image=200802051504181024x768ssy4.png)

Themes:
XFCE - Daloa (comes with Xfce 4.4 beta 2)
GTK - H2O-gtk2-Amythist (it only comes in a [.rpm](http://duncanbrown.org/linux/themes/gnome/repoman/h2o-gtk2-amythist.php) these days... and the misspelling is on the theme's author!)
Icons - [Xubuntu Studio](http://xfce-look.org/content/show.php/XubuntuStudio+Icons?content=65775)
Cursor - Shere_Khan_X
gkrellm - invisible (I always use this...)

Wallpaper: [Inspiration](http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper/details.php?id=1351) by Richard Mohler
Fonts: Lucida Grande all around (8 point bold in titlebar, 8 point regular in gkrellm, 7 point regular elsewhere), except Terminal (DejaVu Sans Mono, 6 point)

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-05
Well shearn89 it's actually that easy that I can just post it here; all you need to do is divide your texboxes into one textbox per info piece. My textbox/iconbox bit looks like this:

```
        iconbox mpd_icon { 
		image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/mpd.png" 
         	mouse { 
                button = "1" 
                command = "spawn" 
                arg = "exec mpc toggle" 
            }
	}
        textbox mpd
        {
            fg = "#bcbcbc"
        }
        iconbox cpu_icon { image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/cpu.png" }
        textbox cpu
        {
            fg = "#bcbcbc"
        }
        iconbox mem_icon { image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/mem.png" }
        textbox mem
        {
            fg = "#bcbcbc"
        }
        iconbox bat_icon { image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/bat.png" }
        textbox battery
        {
            fg = "#bcbcbc"
        }
        textbox date
        {
            fg = "#2079ff"
        }
        textbox time
        {
            fg = "#ff3300"
        }
```

What I might add is that so far I've only seen .png icons to work like this.

### Post by ~LoKe on 2008-02-05
Could I get your scripts for cpu/mem and your bitmaps? :)

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-05
> **~LoKe said:**
> Could I get your scripts for cpu/mem and your bitmaps? :)

Sure, scripts in order:

CPU:
```
`cpufreq-info -mf`
```

Mem:
```
`free -m | grep buffers\/cache | awk '{print $3}'` MiB
```

(thanks to fwojciec for these)

The bitmaps I made myself, some simple replicates without transparancy and background color set to #161616 (my statusbar background). I've uploaded them [here](http://users.telenet.be/gigamo/bitmaps/), the original ones (you will have to convert these to .png yourself in order for them to work though) are [here](http://phraok.free.fr/config/old/dzen/bitmaps/)

Figured I'd post a small update meanwhile.

---

```
#avoid flicker
double_buffer yes
no_buffers yes

own_window yes
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type normal
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

#draw_graph_borders yes
#draw_borders yes

gap_x 1
gap_y 788
alignment bottom_left
  
#behaviour
update_interval 1
  
#colour
#default_color 000000
default_color D6D6D6
#default_color bfbfbf
#default_shade_color 000000
own_window_colour 202020
#draw_borders_colour 000000
#draw_graph_borders_colour 000000
#484432 95956B
  
#font
use_xft yes
xftfont HandelGotD:pixelsize=10
  
#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer no
minimum_size 1278 10
  
#mpd
mpd_host localhost
mpd_port 6600
# ${offset -22}

### Post by urukrama on 2008-02-06
> **Nythain said:**
> Also, is there a way to install gtk themes in fluxbox without the need to install 75% of gnome... all my apps are this ugly grey, its like a flashback to 1995

That was an interesting desktop. I liked the clean white.

I am not sure what you mean by 'installing gtk themes in Fluxbox'. To install a theme, you can just copy it to ~/.themes. For the theme to be applied to your Gtk apps in Fluxbox, you can specify that in the ~/.gtkrc-2.0 file. Here is what you should add to that file (create it if it doesn't exist):


```
# -- THEME AUTO-WRITTEN DO NOT EDIT

include "/home/USERNAME/.themes/THEMENAME/gtk-2.0/gtkrc"

include "/home/USERNAME/.gtkrc.mine"

# -- THEME AUTO-WRITTEN DO NOT EDIT
```

In your ~/.gtkrc.mine file you can specify the Gtk fonts and icons. Here is what mine looks like:

```
style "Fonts"
{
font_name = "Arial Rounded MT 9"
}
widget_class "*" style "Fonts"
gtk-font-name = "Arial Rounded MT 9"

#gtk-icon-theme-name = "GnomeCorsair"
gtk-icon-theme-name = "nuoveXT-1.6"
#gtk-icon-theme-name = "Human_Ultra_Gray"
#gtk-icon-theme-name = "Somatic-O.1.1"
#gtk-icon-theme-name = "DebianIcons"

gtk-toolbar-style = GTK_TOOLBAR_ICONS
```

You can change your Gtk theme and font either by editing these text files, or by using a program like gtk-theme-switch or gtk-chtheme. Icons can only be changed through this text file.

I have written about this at greater length in my [Openbox guide]("http://urukrama.wordpress.com/openbox-guide/"). Some other info in there will also be relevant for Fluxbox users.

---

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-06
> **urukrama said:**
> That was an interesting desktop. I liked the clean white.

I am not sure what you mean by 'installing gtk themes in Fluxbox'. To install a theme, you can just copy it to ~/.themes. For the theme to be applied to your Gtk apps in Fluxbox, you can specify that in the ~/.gtkrc-2.0 file. Here is what you should add to that file (create it if it doesn't exist):


```
# -- THEME AUTO-WRITTEN DO NOT EDIT

include "/home/USERNAME/.themes/THEMENAME/gtk-2.0/gtkrc"

include "/home/USERNAME/.gtkrc.mine"

# -- THEME AUTO-WRITTEN DO NOT EDIT
```

In your ~/.gtkrc.mine file you can specify the Gtk fonts and icons. Here is what mine looks like:

```
style "Fonts"
{
font_name = "Arial Rounded MT 9"
}
widget_class "*" style "Fonts"
gtk-font-name = "Arial Rounded MT 9"

#gtk-icon-theme-name = "GnomeCorsair"
gtk-icon-theme-name = "nuoveXT-1.6"
#gtk-icon-theme-name = "Human_Ultra_Gray"
#gtk-icon-theme-name = "Somatic-O.1.1"
#gtk-icon-theme-name = "DebianIcons"

gtk-toolbar-style = GTK_TOOLBAR_ICONS
```

You can change your Gtk theme and font either by editing these text files, or by using a program like gtk-theme-switch or gtk-chtheme. Icons can only be changed through this text file.

I have written about this at greater length in my [Openbox guide]("http://urukrama.wordpress.com/openbox-guide/"). Some other info in there will also be relevant for Fluxbox users.

Before I drop gnome-settings-daemon, does it do anything else than load the gtk theme? I'm supposing yes, I mean like mouse settings and stuff like that.

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2008-02-06
> **Gigamo said:**
> Before I drop gnome-settings-daemon, does it do anything else than load the gtk theme? I'm supposing yes, I mean like mouse settings and stuff like that.

It also handles your font settings.  However, you can specify them in your ~/.fonts.conf file.

Here is mine as an example:
```
<?xml version="1.0"?>

<!DOCTYPE fontconfig SYSTEM "fonts.dtd">

<fontconfig>
  <match target="font">
    <edit name="antialias" mode="assign"><bool>true</bool></edit>
    <edit name="rgba"      mode="assign"><const>rgb</const></edit>
    <edit name="autohint"  mode="assign"><bool>true</bool></edit>
    <edit name="hintstyle" mode="assign"><const>hintfull</const></edit>
  </match>
  <match target="font">
    <test name="weight" compare="more"><const>medium</const></test>
    <edit name="autohint" mode="assign"><bool>false</bool></edit>
    <edit name="hinting" mode="assign"><bool>false</bool></edit>
    <edit name="hintstyle" mode="assign"><const>hintnone</const></edit>
  </match>
</fontconfig>

```

---

### Post by urukrama on 2008-02-08
> **Nythain said:**
> you all are killin me... kde to fluxbox to awesomewm and now to check out this windowlab... hehe... looks minimal and slick... i like

Windowlab is quite minimal, but if you like configuring your window manager to the extreme, it isn't for you. You can change the colours and the menu, but that is about it. Unless you hack the program, you can't change the default keybindings or window decorations. Windowlab is also rather limited in functionality (no virtual desktops, no shading of windows, etc.). But I rather like it :) (for simple tasks at least).

> **ayoli said:**
> Nifty :)

Thanks :D

> **shearn89 said:**
> Windowlab looks cool - kinda like awesome without the tiling, from what i read on the [website]("http://nickgravgaard.com/windowlab/").

It is less functional and less customizable than Awesome.

> **shearn89 said:**
> For black icon themes, you could take a dark icon theme, desaturate it to black and white in gimp, and amess with the contrast? Something like the area04 icons would look good in b+w...

Thanks for the suggestion, but I don't want to spend as much time on an icon theme I'll rarely use. My default dark icon theme is GnomeCorsair, which is great but not black-black. I rarely want to use a pitch black icon theme.

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-09
> **fedex1993 said:**
> how did you change htops color and stuff from the default color? also could i get your screenrc again

htop's color can be changed by pressing F10 (setup) in htop.

Screenrc:

```
defflow auto
#defmonitor on
defscrollback 10000
altscreen on
autodetach on
msgwait 2 # 1 second messages
shell /bin/zsh

hardstatus alwayslastline '%{= W} %H%{= B} %l %= %{= w}%-w%{+b W}%n*%t%{-b B}%{w}%+w %= %{W}%d %D %{B}%c '

vbell_msg "[[[ ding ]]]"
vbell on
startup_message off
setenv LC_CTYPE en_US.UTF-8

#screen -t 'htop' htop
screen -t 'torrent' rtorrent
screen -t 'rss' snownews -u
screen -t 'irc' irssi
screen -t 'zsh' zsh

bind k
bind W
bind ^k
bind .
bind ^\
bind \\
bind ^h
bind h
bind 'K' kill
bind 'W' windowlist
      
bindkey -k k1 prev
bindkey -k k2 next  
```

You may have to remove the "shell /bin/zsh" line if you are using bash instead of zsh.

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-09
> **shearn89 said:**
> @Gigamo - how do you find zsh? i've got it installed, but haven't got into scripting with it yet.

edit: ooh, beer. (half a one found on my desk under some stuff).

I like it that much that I have made it my default shell. It does everything bash does, but more :). I love the spelling correction for one, here's an example of that:

```
gig@giGnote> gedit .awesoemrc                                                                                                                       ~
zsh: correct '.awesoemrc' to '.awesomerc' [nyae]? 

```

That and I have a very good .zshrc I picked up somewhere.

zsh: correct '.awesoemrc' to '.awesomerc' [nyae]? 

```

That and I have a very good .zshrc I picked up somewhere.

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-09
> **shearn89 said:**
> nice. can i nab your .zshrc? mine isn't great, and so far i haven't found anything major to make me switch. perhaps some consistent usage would work?

Sure;

```
# zsh enviroment -------------------------------------------------------

export BROWSER="firefox3"
export EDITOR="vim"
export VISUAL=$EDITOR
export MAIL="~/.mail"
export NNTPSERVER="newsgroups.bellsouth.net"
export PATH=${PATH}:/usr/local/bin:/usr/local/games


# modules --------------------------------------------------------------

zstyle :compinstall filename '/home/gig/.zshrc'

autoload -U colors compinit promptinit
colors
compinit
promptinit; prompt walters

zmodload zsh/mathfunc
zmodload zsh/complist


# terminal -------------------------------------------------------------

if [[ "$TERM" = "rxvt-unicode" ]]; then
     export TERM="rxvt"
fi

# set terminal title
case $TERM in
     xterm*|rxvt*|screen)
          precmd () {print -Pn "\e]0;%n@%m: %~\a"}
     ;;
esac

if [[ -f /etc/DIR_COLORS ]]; then
     eval `dircolors -b /etc/DIR_COLORS`
fi


# settings -------------------------------------------------------------

bindkey -v
bindkey "^r" history-incremental-search-backward

umask 077
ulimit -S -c 0
HISTFILE=~/.histfile
HISTSIZE=200
SAVEHIST=200

setopt append_history share_history extended_history
setopt hist_ignore_all_dups hist_expire_dups_first hist_find_no_dups
setopt hist_verify bang_hist hist_ignore_space inc_append_history

setopt autopushd pushdminus pushdsilent pushdtohome nopromptcr
setopt notify noclobber autolist rcquotes interactivecomments
setopt autocd correct correctall extendedglob dvorak globdots

setopt alwaystoend completeinword cdablevars chase_links numeric_glob_sort
setopt autoresume check_jobs long_list_jobs


# completion -----------------------------------------------------------

zstyle ':completion::complete:*' use-cache on
zstyle ':completion::complete:*' cache-path ~/.zsh/cache
zstyle ':completion:*' _force_rehash

zstyle ':completion:*:*:kill:*:processes' list-colors "=(#b) #([0-9]#)*=36=31"
zstyle ':completion:*' list-colors "$LS_COLORS"
zstyle ':completion:*:*:kill:*' menu yes select
zstyle ':completion:*:kill:*' force-list always

zstyle ':completion:*:processes' command 'ps -U $(whoami) | sed "/ps/d"'
zstyle ':completion:*:processes' insert-ids menu yes select 

zstyle ':completion:*:functions' ignored-patterns '_*'

zstyle -e ':completion:*:approximate:*' \
          max-errors 'reply=($((($#PREFIX+$#SUFFIX)/3))numeric)'
zstyle ':completion:*' completer _complete _match _approximate
zstyle ':completion:*:match:*' original only
zstyle ':completion:*:approximate:*' max-errors 1 numeric
zstyle ':completion:*' expand 'yes'
zstyle ':completion:*' squeeze-slashes 'yes'

zstyle ':completion:*' menu select
zstyle ':completion:*' verbose yes
zstyle ':completion:*:descriptions' format '%B%d%b'
zstyle ':completion:*:messages' format '%d'
zstyle ':completion:*:warnings' format 'No matches for: %d'
zstyle ':completion:*:corrections' format '%B%d (errors: %e)%b'
zstyle ':completion:*' select-prompt %SScrolling active: current selection at %p%s
zstyle ':completion:*' group-name ''

zstyle ':completion:*:(cd|mv|cp):*' ignore-parents parent pwd
zstyle ':completion:*:(rm|kill|diff):*' ignore-line yes

# match uppercase from lowercase
zstyle ':completion:*' matcher-list 'm:{a-z}={A-Z}'

# Add known hosts to SSH completion
zstyle -e ':completion:*:(ssh|scp):*' hosts 'reply=(
     ${=${${(f)"$(cat {/etc/ssh_,~/.ssh/known_}hosts(|2)(N) \
     /dev/null)"}%%[# ]*}//,/ }
     )'

zstyle ':completion:*:*:*:users' ignored-patterns \
     bin bitlbee daemon dbus fetchmail ftp hal mail mpd nobody \
     postfix privoxy sshd tor


# aliases --------------------------------------------------------------

alias -s gz="tar -xzvf"
alias -s bz2="tar -xjvf"
alias -s zip="unzip"
alias -s rar="rar x"

alias -s {jpg,jpeg,png,gif}="feh --scale-down"
alias -s {mp3,ogg,wav,flac}="mplayer"
alias -s {mpg,mpeg,avi,ogm,wmv,m4v,mp4,mov,mkv}="mplayer"
alias -s {html,php,com,net,org,gov}=$BROWSER
alias -s txt=$EDITOR
alias -s doc="catdoc"
alias -s pdf="epdfview"
alias -s xcf="gimp-remote"

alias -g ...="../.."
alias -g ....="../../.."
alias -g .....="../../../.."

alias -g L="|less"
alias -g G="|grep"
alias -g H="|head"
alias -g T="|tail"
alias -g S="|sort"

alias halt="sudo /sbin/halt"
alias reboot="sudo reboot"
alias :q="exit"
alias :wq="exit"
alias bbs="mrxvt --font smoothansi -bg black -fg white -e telnet REMOVED"
alias bc="bc -q"
alias c='clear'
alias cp="nocorrect cp -v"
alias du="du -h --max-depth=1"
alias df="df -h"
alias e=$EDITOR
alias grep="grep --color=auto -n"
alias h="history"
alias ht="htop -u $(whoami) -t"
alias j="jobs"
alias k="kill"
alias l="ls"
alias ls="ls -hF --color=auto -a"
alias mkdir='nocorrect mkdir'
alias mv="nocorrect mv -v"
alias netstat="netstat -nap --inet"
alias nzb="hellanzb.py"
alias pgrep="pgrep -l"
alias q="exit"
alias rm="nocorrect rm -v"
alias recent="ls -lAt | head"
alias screen="screen -R"
alias ss="scrot %Y-%m-%d_moparx.png -d 8 -c -t 576x230"
alias start="dbus-launch startx -nolisten tcp"
alias syn="rsync -avz -e ssh --exclude-from=/home/moparx/.rsync/exclude --delete --delete-excluded /home/moparx moparx@REMOVED:/home/moparx/backups"
alias today='date "+%A, %d %B, %G%t%H:%M %Z(%z)"'
alias urxvt="urxvtc"
alias vi="vim"
alias vd="vimdiff"
alias install="sudo aptitude install"
alias remove="sudo aptitude purge"
alias aptup="sudo apt-get update && sudo aptitude upgrade"
alias show="aptitude show"
alias search="aptitude search"

# functions ------------------------------------------------------------

bashorg () {
     w3m -dump "http://www.bash.org/?${1}" |less
}   

makepasswords() {
     perl <<EOPERL
          my @a = ("a".."z","A".."Z","0".."9",(split //, q{#@,.<>$%&()*^}));
          for (1..10) {
               print join "", map { \$a[rand @a] } (1..rand(3)+10);
               print qq{\n}
          }
EOPERL
}

_force_rehash()
{
     (( CURRENT == 1 )) && rehash
     return 1
}

src () {
     autoload -U zrecompile
     [ -f ~/.zshrc ] && zrecompile -p ~/.zshrc
     [ -f ~/.zcompdump ] && zrecompile -p ~/.zcompdump
     [ -f ~/.zshrc.zwc.old ] && rm -f ~/.zshrc.zwc.old
     [ -f ~/.zcompdump.zwc.old ] && rm -f ~/.zcompdump.zwc.old
     source ~/.zshrc
}

```

### Post by urukrama on 2008-02-12
Here is an update to my previous desktop. I've made some minor adjustments to the Gtk theme. 

I've changed some of the icons of the areo set too, so they match my theme better. One of the things I always disliked in the areo set was that all files had the same icon. I have therefore changed most of the mime-type icons, so that the icon now shows what file type they represent (see the second screenshot). I'm not too happy with the folder icon yet, but it'll do for now.

I still need to figure out where to put a system tray. I don't want to include it in pypanel, as I like the simple and clean look it has now. Other than that, I like this desktop. :)

Feedback is welcome.

### Post by ayoli on 2008-02-13
> **Nythain said:**
> And now for my latest...
This time around its gnome... spent days on top of days just trying to figure this DE/WM out...
Terminal has most of the details, except it has my terminal font wrong... as you can see, the terminal font is also Century Schoolbook L
I cant seem to get away from conky... its about the most simple and informative lightweight app i can find for its purpose... If only it had interface interactivity like SuperKaramba... in fact, if i could ever get the look/effect of Conky with the Scripting/Interactivity of SuperKaramba, in gnome, i would probably die of to much ecstasy (the joy type, not the drug type :P )

Also, does anyone know how to achieve a transparent borderless gnome-terminal (or any terminal in gnome for that matter) that will stay onbottom of everything??? Devilspie doesnt play well with Gutsy's desktop effects (compiz???)

If you use the desktops effects you can do this easily. Go ti menu system>preferences>advanced desktop effects settings.
if you don't have this : sudo apt-get install compizconfig-settings-manager )
Then in effects section select "windows decorations"
in the field "decoration windows" put this:
```
!(name=gnome-terminal)
```

Transparency can be set in the gnome-terminal settings.

edit: oops didn't see you've manage to do this :)

---

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2008-02-13
Yes, it's just a program that prints out matrix-ish text in a terminal
```
sudo apt-get install cmatrix
```
Then you can run it with 
```
cmatrix
```

### Post by ayoli on 2008-02-14
> **PurposeOfReason said:**
> Do I look like a pansy? lol

Everything except the fingerprint scanner is golden. The battery could do a bit better and the wireless light doesn't show up when it's activated (by very few vaios do anyways). It was a good day. :) Xdefaults sent.

you can create a file named with the name of your wireless module (in /etc/modeprobe.d/ on ubuntu, you should have an equivalent for arch) and put in :
```
options led=1
```

### Post by sunexplodes on 2008-02-14
Here's today's modification.

[ATTACH]59646[/ATTACH]

DE: KDEmod
WM: Emerald (Modified version of Emerald Brit, attached)
STYLE: Domino
FONTS: Lucida family, Heldustry for titlebar (included in attachment)
WALLPAPER: Futublu

The modification of the Elegant Brit Emerald theme (created by forum member What's In A Name? if I recall correctly) consists of: visible close/restore/minimize buttons on the active window, tweaked shadows, different title font/alignment, and a small change to the window border size).

[ATTACH]59647[/ATTACH]

They look different to me, lol. Here is the relevant part of my xdefaults.

urxvt.font:             xft:Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:pixelsize=8
urxvt.boldFont:         xft:Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:bold:pixelsize=9

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-16
> **rjmdomingo2003 said:**
> Would you care to share your awesomerc & awesome-monitor, Gigs? Thanks!

awesomerc:

```

screen 0
{
    general
    {
        border = 1
        snap = 8
        resize_hints = true
        opacity_unfocused = 100
        #focus_move_pointer = false
        new_get_focus = true
        new_become_master = false
        #allow_lower_floats = false
        font = "Dejavu Sans Mono-6.10"
    }

    colors
    {
        normal_border = "#222222"
        normal_bg = "#222222"
        normal_fg = "#dddddd"
        focus_border = "#333333"
        focus_bg = "#303030"
        focus_fg = "#99ccff"
        urgent_bg = "#0066ff"
        urgent_fg = "#dddddd"
        tab_border = "#ff0000"
    }

    tags
    {
        tag 1:main { layout = "tile" }
        tag 2:web { layout = "tilebottom" }
        tag 3:edit { layout = "tile" }
        tag 4:other { layout = "floating" }
    }

    layouts
    {
        layout tile { image = "/usr/local/share/awesome/icons/layouts/tilew.png" }
        layout tileleft { image = "/usr/local/share/awesome/icons/layouts/tileleftw.png" }
        layout tilebottom { image = "/usr/local/share/awesome/icons/layouts/tilebottomw.png" }
        layout tileup { image = "/usr/local/share/awesome/icons/layouts/tileupw.png" }
        layout max { image = "/usr/local/share/awesome/icons/layouts/maxw.png" }
        layout spiral { image = "/usr/local/share/awesome/icons/layouts/spiralw.png" }
        layout dwindle { image = "/usr/local/share/awesome/icons/layouts/dwindlew.png" }
        layout floating { image = "/usr/local/share/awesome/icons/layouts/floatingw.png" }
    }

    statusbar top
    {
        position = "top"
        height = "16"
        
        taglist tl
        {
            mouse
            {
                button = "1"
                command = "tag_view"
            }
            mouse
            {
                button = "1"
                modkey = {"Mod4"}
                command = "client_tag"
            }
            mouse
            {
                button = "3"
                command = "tag_toggleview"
            }
            mouse
            {
                button = "3"
                modkey = {"Mod4"}
                command = "client_toggletag"
            }
            mouse
            {
                button = "4"
                command = "tag_viewnext"
            }
            mouse
            {
                button = "5"
                command = "tag_viewprev"
            }
        }

        layoutinfo li
        {
            mouse
            {
                button = "1"
                command = "tag_setlayout"
                arg = "+1"
            }
            mouse
            {
                button = "4"
                command = "tag_setlayout"
                arg = "+1"
            }
            mouse
            {
                button = "3"
                command = "tag_setlayout"
                arg = "-1"
            }
            mouse
            {
                button = "5"
                command = "tag_setlayout"
                arg = "-1"
            }
        }

        #tasklist tasktop
        #{
        #    show = "focused"
        #    show_icons = "false"
        #}

        iconbox mpd_prev
        {
            image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/cool/pre.png"
            mouse
            {
                button = "1"
                command = "spawn"
                arg = "exec mpc prev"
            }
            align = "right"
        }
        iconbox mpd_play
        {
            image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/cool/pp.png"
            mouse
            {
                button = "1"
                command = "spawn"
                arg = "exec mpc toggle"
            }
            align = "right"
        }
        iconbox mpd_next
        {
            image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/cool/next.png"
            mouse
            {
                button = "1"
                command = "spawn"
                arg = "exec mpc next"
            }
            align = "right"
        }
        textbox mpd
        {
            fg = "#bbbbbb"
            mouse { button = "1" command = "spawn" arg = "urxvtc -e ncmpc" }
            align = "right"
        }
        textbox sep1 { text =  "· " fg = "#dddddd" align = "right" }
        iconbox mem_icon { image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/cool/mem.png" align = "right" }
        textbox mem { fg = "#bbbbbb" align = "right" }
        progressbar pb_mem
        {
            bar { fg = "#F0E68C" bg = "#A7A15E" bordercolor = "#5F3A22" }
            width = "50"
            height = "0.6"
            gap = 2
            padding = 3
            align = "right"
        }
        textbox sep2 { text =  "·" fg = "#dddddd" align = "right" }
        textbox battery { fg = "#bbbbbb" align = "right" }
        textbox sep3 { text =  "· " fg = "#dddddd" align = "right" }
        iconbox mail_icon { image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/mail2.png" align = "right" }
        textbox mail { fg = "#bbbbbb" align = "right" }
        textbox sep4 { text =  "·" fg = "#dddddd" align = "right" }
        textbox datum { fg = "#bbbbbb" align = "right" }
        textbox tijd { fg = "#99ccff" align = "right" }
        textbox sep5 { text = " · " fg = "#dddddd" align = "right" }
        iconbox mpd_volume
        {
            image = "/home/gig/.bitmaps/cool/vol.png"
            mouse
            {
                button = "4"
                command = "spawn"
                arg = "exec amixer -c0 sset Front 2dB+ >/dev/null"
            }
            mouse
            {
                button = "5"
                command = "spawn"
                arg = "exec amixer -c0 sset Front 2dB- >/dev/null"
            }
            align = "right"
        }
        progressbar pb_vol
        {
            bar { fg = "#7c96b0" bg = "#364a57" bordercolor = "#274e84" }
            width = "30"
            height = "0.6"
            gap = 2
            padding = 3
            align = "right"
        }
    }

    statusbar bottom
    {
        position = "bottom"
        height = "16"
        
        tasklist taskbottom
        {
            show_icons = "false"
            show = "all"

            x = 1
            y = 0

            mouse
            {
                modkey = {}
                button = "4"
                command = "client_focusnext"
            }
            mouse
            {
                modkey = {}
                button = "5"
                command = "client_focusprev"
            }
            mouse
            {
                modkey = {"Mod4"}
                button = "4"
                command = "client_swapnext"
            }
            mouse
            {
                modkey = {"Mod4"}
                button = "5"
                command = "client_swapprev"
            }
        }
    }
}

    rules
    {
        rule { name = "Gimp" tags = "3:edit" float = "true" }
        rule { name = "Pidgin" tags = "1:main" float = "true" }
        rule { name = "Deluge" tags = "4:other" }
        #rule { name = "Thunar" float = "true" }
        rule { name = "Mirage" float = "true" }
        rule { name = "xfrun4" float = "true" }
        rule { name = "VLC" float = "true" }
        rule { name = "gvim" tags = "3:edit" float = "false" }
        rule { name = "urxvt" }
        rule { name = "Swiftweasel" tags = "2:web" }
    }

    mouse
    {
        root
        {
            button = "4"
            command = "tag_viewnext"
        }
        root
        {
            button = "5"
            command = "tag_viewprev"
        }
        client

            modkey = {"Mod1"}
            button = "1"
            command = "client_movemouse"
        }
        client
        {
            modkey = {"Mod1"}
            button = "2"
            command = "client_zoom"
        }

            button = "3"
            command = "client_resizemouse"
        }
    }

```

awesome-monitor:

```

#!/bin/sh

while true
do
echo 0 widget_tell mpd " `mpc | sed -n '1p'` " | /usr/local/bin/awesome-client
echo 0 widget_tell mem " `free -m | grep buffers\/cache | awk '{print $3}'`MiB " | /usr/local/bin/awesome-client
echo 0 widget_tell battery " `acpi -b | awk '{print $3, $4}' | sed -e s/,//2` " | /usr/local/bin/awesome-client
echo 0 widget_tell mail " `sh '.scripts/check_gmail.sh'` " | /usr/local/bin/awesome-client
echo 0 widget_tell datum " `date '+%a %b %d'`"| /usr/local/bin/awesome-client
echo 0 widget_tell tijd " `date '+%H:%M'`" | /usr/local/bin/awesome-client
echo 0 widget_tell pb_vol "`amixer sget Front | grep 'Left: Playback' | awk '{print $6}' | sed 's/\[//g;s/%\]//g'`" | /usr/local/bin/awesome-client
sleep 1
done

```

I've rewritten the awesomerc from scratch for 2.2, the things that are commented with # are things that worked in 2.1 and no longer in 2.2, so I would leave them that way or just delete :)

And I am still working on the progressbar pb_mem, so it won't show any info just yet :p

### Post by Freddy on 2008-02-17
> **sunexplodes said:**
> Here's today's modification.

[ATTACH]59646[/ATTACH]

DE: KDEmod
WM: Emerald (Modified version of Emerald Brit, attached)
STYLE: Domino

WALLPAPER: Futublu

The modification of the Elegant Brit Emerald theme (created by forum member What's In A Name? if I recall correctly) consists of: visible close/restore/minimize buttons on the active window, tweaked shadows, different title font/alignment, and a small change to the window border size).

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2008-02-17
> **Freddy said:**
> How do I install that modded Elegant emerald theme?
You just extract it to ~/.emerald/themes

If you've already installed others, you can see how it should look when you get it in there
You should have a folder called
~/.emerald/themes/themename

Also, you can just rename the file to ElegantBritMod.emerald and use emerald-theme-manager to install it

### Post by pppoe_dude on 2008-02-17
Hi!
Here is a website that hosts linux screenshots - **[www.xshot.org](www.xshot.org)** 
You can host your full sized screenshot there and it will provide you with a smaller version too. There is also a tagging tool so you can specify which programs are running, etc... 

It's still in early stages so please send your feedback!

---

### Post by thecapuchin on 2008-02-17
> **raul_ said:**
> Did you change KDE style? You must have domino installed

I didn't do anything with domino, all I did was run

```
kcontrol
```

in a terminal which resulted in the attached screenshot.  Expand Appearance and Themes, click on Colors then click on Import Scheme, browse to the .kcsrc file and you're good to go.

### Post by thecapuchin on 2008-02-17
> **jordanmthomas said:**
> That's fluxbox and its menu.
There's a package called menu and one called xdg-menu that will generate menus like that.

(I didn't post this, so if I'm wrong feel free to correct me)

Awesome, thanks for the info.

> **Opeth115 said:**
> Is that my color scheme i posted?

Is there anyway to make my menu's in KDE transparent with compiz liek you can in gnome?  Also how can i change the link to my terminal in my right click menu, or update it?  I set my terminal to use true transparency, but the link in the default right click menu for kdemod doesn't update to the same one in the start menu...

Yes, I believe it is the one you posted a few pages back.  Thanks much!

As for getting dropdown menu opacity changed, I believe that you can check in the compiz advance configuration and check the General Options module.  In there, there should be a tab for Opacity Settings.  Click on that, and under Window Opacities you can edit the value of the entry there.  Adding DropdownMenu to the list (separated with a | ) should add the opcaity you're looking for.  I think the screenshots I've attached should illustrate how it works in gnome at least.  I would imagine that KDE wouldn't be terribly different.

---

### Post by Opeth115 on 2008-02-17

As for getting dropdown menu opacity changed, I believe that you can check in the compiz advance configuration and check the General Options module.  In there, there should be a tab for Opacity Settings.  Click on that, and under Window Opacities you can edit the value of the entry there.  Adding DropdownMenu to the list (separated with a | ) should add the opcaity you're looking for.  I think the screenshots I've attached should illustrate how it works in gnome at least.  I would imagine that KDE wouldn't be terribly different.

### Post by thecapuchin on 2008-02-17
> **Opeth115 said:**
> Sweet that worked, but it isn't consistant, every like second click it turns the menu transparent, not on the first time.  So i have to click the start button twice for it to be transparent, is that just a bug?  And would u happen to know hwo i can edit that link to my console in my right click menu?

On the first point, I don't know if it's a bug that the menus don't come up translucent the first time, but I'm pretty sure that it works on my machine at home (currently connected from work or I'd check - no 3d effects through ssh).

As for the second, I believe the way to edit which terminal is opened by the link in the right click menu is to go into Preferred Applications and set which terminal you want the system to use.

### Post by epimer on 2008-02-18
> **Opeth115 said:**
> And would u happen to know hwo i can edit that link to my console in my right click menu?

How I did it was to right-click the menu button, Menu Editor, click on the entry for konsole and change the Command to "konsole --real-transparency" (without the quotes, obviously). Now when I launch konsole from either the K Menu or with katapult, it's properly transparent.

Screenshot to demonstrate the above, and I guess theme details while I'm at it. Have had the same setup for a while now, because I'm comfortable with it, I suppose.

DE: KDEmod on Arch
Style: QTCurve
Icons: KDEmod Tango
Wallpaper: It's called "bluestreak", and I suspect I got it from deviantart.
Emerald theme:  tweaked Azurite-Studio.
Colour scheme: paper-ink

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-18
> **Chipter said:**
> That looks cool.
how did you get the taskbars to look like that?
where can I download awesome?

The taskbars are part of the awesome window manager, which can be gotten here: [http://awesome.naquadah.org/](http://awesome.naquadah.org/)

The status info in the top bar is a bit more complicated.

There is also some excellent guides from LoKe and shearn89 on this forum for setting up awesome, but only for the 2.1 version. I am using the latest 2.2 RC. The difference between them both is almost none though except for a few new features.

---

Yep that's me. 

I think that if you scale panel-bg.png to the height of your panel, it should be fine. I just used 24px bitmaps because (afaik) that's the default gnome-panel height. I imagine that the menubar is "reading" the image from a different starting point than the panel, thus they don't line up.

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2008-02-19
> **arbulus said:**
> I've seen a lot of people here using urxvt for a terminal and it looks really neat, with all the different colors and whatnot.  But when I installed it and ran it, everything was really ugly and grey.  Are there some kind of config files for it that you have to set to make is so colorful?
That's all in the ~/.Xdefaults file. Here is mine as I see many of them are based off of it. 
```

URxvt.termName: rxvt
URxvt.transparent: true
URxvt.inheritPixmap: False
URxvt.imLocale: pl_PL.UTF-8
URxvt.scrollBar: false
URxvt.saveLines: 5000
URxvt.urlLauncher:      firefox3
URxvt.cursorBlink: false
URxvt.geometry: 85x21
URxvt.fading: 45%
URxvt.shading: 75
urxvt.font:             xft:Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:pixelsize=8
urxvt.boldFont:         xft:Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:bold:pixelsize=9
!URxvt*background:      #000000
urxvt.depth: 32
urxvt.background: rgba:0000/0000/0000/aaaa
urxvt.foreground: rgba:ffff/ffff/ffff/aaaa
!URxvt.foreground: #ffffff
URxvt.tintColor: #262626
URxvt.borderLess: true
URxvt.borderColor: #000000
URxvt.externalBorder: 1
!URxvt.internalBorder: 25

*foreground:     rgba:1000/1000/1000/aaaa
*background:     rgb:10/10/10
!black
*color0:         rgb:20/20/20
*color8:         rgb:75/77/73
!red
*color1:         rgb:cc/00/00  
*color9:         rgb:ef/29/29
!green
*color2:         rgb:4e/9a/06
*color10:        rgb:8a/e2/34
!brown/yellow
*color3:         rgb:c4/a0/00
*color11:        rgb:fc/e9/4f
!blue
*color4:         rgb:34/65/a4
*color12:        rgb:72/9f/cf
!magenta
*color5:         rgb:75/50/7b
*color13:        rgb:ad/7f/a8
!cyan
*color6:         rgb:06/98/9a
*color14:        rgb:34/e2/e2
!white
*color7:         rgb:d3/d7/cf
*color15:        rgb:ee/ee/ec

```

Oops... Sorry for that... I'll check it out... Thanks for the tip!

EDIT: When I try to install the artwiz-fonts, there is a message complaining about a missing directory inside of /usr/lib/X11... Should I create that missing directory? The system says the package is installed, anyway, but I can't seem to find Gelly anywhere even though I refreshed the cache.

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2008-02-20
They are not scalable fonts, but bit-mapped ones.  So you have to have fontconfig configured to allow them and you also need to add the artwiz font directory to your /etc/X11/xorg.conf file in a FontPath statement.  (and you have to restart X afterwards)  :D

Also, several of the font packages in Ubuntu cause that missing directory message.  When I was running Ubuntu, I created a symbolic link in the /usr/lib/X11 directory that pointed back into /usr/share/fonts/X11 (or something like that), and it cleared it up.

---

> Here is a somewhat disturbing snapshot of my Kubuntu 7.10 with Windows Vista Home Premium running (surprisingly well!) in a VirtualBox virtual machine.  I installed Vista from the OEM disk that came with my laptop.

Ha! I like it!! Kinda cool how you just neglected the taskbar applet. I cant tell by the icon theme but im assuming you use a window list applet to manage open windows, yeah? Pretty cool though...

Careful- I wouldnt install updates on Vista, at least if you still dual-boot. Just a good AV and spyware, or even better dont use vista for any web access. Its technically not legal for you to run the OEM version both on the machine and as a VM- youd need to purchase a second copy (I know its gay- its your disc on the same computer :/ )

We could have dealt without Vista in the screenshot :) We dont really wanna see it ;)

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-02-21
> **fedex1993 said:**
> how did you get transparency working looks very nice

xcompmgr and these Xdefaults:

```
urxvt.font: xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=10
urxvt*geometry:    80x25
urxvt*saveLines:   2048
urxvt*scrollBar:	    false
urxvt*scrollstyle:	    plain   ! options: rxvt, plain, next or xterm. plain
urxvt*scrollBar_right:	    true
urxvt*borderColor:      rgba:0000/0000/0000/aaaa
urxvt*loginShell:	    true
urxvt*internalBorder:	    3
urxvt*depth: 32
urxvt*background:	rgba:0000/0000/0000/aaaa
urxvt*foreground:       #dddddd
urxvt.borderLess:         true
urxvt*termName:		    rxvt
urxvt*cutchars:		    "()*,<>[]{}|'
urxvt*print-pipe:	    cat > $(echo urxvt.dump.`date +'%Y%M%d%H%m%S'`)
urxvt*secondaryScroll:	    true
urxvt*mapAlert:		    true
urxvt*utmpInhibit:	    true
urxvt*perl-lib:		    /usr/lib/urxvt/perl/
urxvt*perl-ext-common:	    default,matcher
urxvt*urlLauncher:	    swtrunk
urxvt*matcher.button:	    1
urxvt*matcher.pattern.1:   \\bwww\\.[\\w-]+\\.[\\w./?&@#-]*[\\w/-]
urxvt*visualBell:	    true

*cursorColor:    #ffcc00
urxvt*cursorBlink: true

*background:     rgb:12/12/12
```

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2008-02-21
> **Gigamo said:**
> Mind sharing the wallpaper/your xdefaults colors? :)
The xdefaults have hardly changed:
```
URxvt.termName: rxvt
URxvt.transparent: true
URxvt.inheritPixmap: False
URxvt.imLocale: pl_PL.UTF-8
URxvt.scrollBar: false
URxvt.saveLines: 5000
URxvt.urlLauncher:      firefox3
URxvt.cursorBlink: false
URxvt.geometry: 85x21
URxvt.fading: 45%
URxvt.shading: 75
urxvt.font:             xft:Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:pixelsize=8
urxvt.boldFont:         xft:Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:bold:pixelsize=9
!URxvt*background:      #000000
urxvt.depth: 32
urxvt.background: rgba:0000/0000/0000/aaaa
urxvt.foreground: rgba:ffff/ffff/ffff/aaaa
!URxvt.foreground: #ffffff
URxvt.tintColor: #262626
URxvt.borderLess: true
URxvt.InternalBorder: 25
URxvt.borderColor: #fafafa

*foreground:     rgba:1000/1000/1000/aaaa
*background:     rgb:10/10/10
!black
*color0:         rgb:20/20/20
*color8:         rgb:75/77/73
!red
*color1:         rgb:cc/00/00  
*color9:         rgb:ef/29/29
!green
*color2:         rgb:4e/9a/06
*color10:        rgb:8a/e2/34
!brown/yellow
*color3:         rgb:c4/a0/00
*color11:        rgb:fc/e9/4f
!blue
*color4:         rgb:34/65/a4
*color12:        rgb:72/9f/cf
!magenta
*color5:         rgb:75/50/7b
*color13:        rgb:ad/7f/a8
!cyan
*color6:         rgb:06/98/9a
*color14:        rgb:34/e2/e2
!white
*color7:         rgb:d3/d7/cf
*color15:        rgb:ee/ee/ec

```

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2008-02-23
> **fedex1993 said:**
> Wow very nice desktop i wish mine looked as good as yours what s that little game your playing in the bottom right also can i get your conky config without the gmail stuff
The game is moon-buggy. It should be in the Ubuntu repos, I mean, it's just a terminal game. The conky config, I have two but I'll assume you don't want the arch updates one. It's actually very long as it will reflect if I'm connected to the internet and which device I'm using.

~/.conkyrc
```

 #avoid flicker
double_buffer yes

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
own_window  yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type override
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

background true

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 3

#shades
draw_shades no

#position
gap_x 5
gap_y 5
alignment bottom_left

#behaviour
update_interval 3

#color
default_color  000000
color1 d1d1d1
color2 d1d1d1

#font
use_xft yes
xftfont Myriad Pro:pixelsize=14

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer yes

#mpd
mpd_host localhost
mpd_port 6600

minimum_size 1280 5
maximum_width 1280 30

TEXT
//Core1 ${color1}${cpu cpu1}%${color}   //Core2 ${color1}${cpu cpu2}%${color}   //Memory ${color1}${memperc}%${color}   //Battery ${color1}${battery_percent BAT1}%${color}${if_existing /sys/class/net/wlan0/operstate up}    //Upload ${color1}${upspeed wlan0}kb/s${color}   //Download ${color1}${downspeed wlan0}kb/s${color}   //Signal ${color1}${wireless_link_qual_perc wlan0}${color}${else}${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}    //Upload ${color1}${upspeed eth0}kb/s${color}   //Download ${color1}${downspeed eth0}kb/s${color}${else}${endif}${endif}${if_existing /sys/class/net/wlan0/operstate up}   //Mail ${color1}${execi 300 python ~/.scripts/gmail.py}${color}${else}${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}    //Mail ${color1}${execi 300 python ~/.scripts/gmail.py}${else}${endif}${endif} ${alignr}${color}//${color2}${time %m.%e.%G}${color}    //${color2}${time %l.%M}${color}   

```
